Implement the following plan:

# CI Gate + Replay Pipeline Consolidation

## Context

There is no working CI gate. The `just ci` recipe is broken (references removed PlatformIO envs) and incomplete (missing codegen check, GCS tests). The replay binary (`replay_main.cpp`) reimplements the flight loop pipeline and has drifted — it's missing `AccelMeasurementUpdate()` and `SymmetrizeCovariance()`, causing the EKF to diverge on ArduPilot logs. The ArduPilot replay export also writes `hacc_m=0`, but that only affects the live flight loop path (which gates on hacc), not the replay binary.

The fix: eliminate the duplicate pipeline. The replay binary becomes just another HAL — same `FlightLoop`, same snapshots, same log format. The analysis tool reads the standard log independently.

## Part 1: FullEkf — add missing methods

`FlightLoop` calls 4 methods that `FullEkf` doesn't have. All must be implemented (not stubbed) so both EKFs run identically through the flight loop.

### 1a. `InitAttitudeOnly(const ImuSample& imu)` — ~30 lines
Mirror `SmolEkf::InitAttitudeOnly` (smol_ekf.cpp:394-430). FullEkf version must also call `AllocateMatrices()` first (since FullEkf uses heap-allocated Eigen matrices). Logic: gravity leveling from accel, zero heading, zero biases, configure LPFs.

### 1b. `ResetPositionVelocity(const GpsSample& gps)` — ~15 lines
Mirror `SmolEkf::ResetPositionVelocity` (smol_ekf.cpp:486-503). Set position/velocity states from GPS, zero the first 6 rows/cols of P, reinitialize pos/vel diagonal, call `UpdateWmmField`, reset baro.

### 1c. `AccelMeasurementUpdate()` — ~30 lines
Gravity fusion is real estimation math — FullEkf must implement it properly using its dense Kalman formulation (full H matrix, full K computation via `ApplyKalmanGain()`), NOT by copying SmolEkf's sequential scalar shortcut. Same gate logic (0.9g–1.1g), same H_att = 2·Sk(accel_predicted), but use FullEkf's existing dense update machinery: build H (3×21, nonzero at cols 6:8), R (3×3 diagonal), compute K, apply Joseph-form P update.

### 1d. `SymmetrizeCovariance()` — no-op
FullEkf's dense Joseph-form updates preserve symmetry mathematically. Implement as empty method so `FlightLoop` can call it unconditionally on both EKF types.

### Files
- `src/estimation/full_ekf.h` — add 4 public method declarations
- `src/estimation/full_ekf.cpp` — add 4 implementations

## Part 2: `#ifdef` EKF selection in flight_loop.h

Add a compile-time switch so the native binary can use either EKF:

```cpp
#ifdef USE_FULL_EKF
#include "estimation/full_ekf.h"
using Ekf = FullEkf;
#else
#include "estimation/smol_ekf.h"
using Ekf = SmolEkf;
#endif
```

Change `SmolEkf _ekf;` → `Ekf _ekf;` in the `FlightLoop` class.

Add a second PlatformIO environment `env:native_full_ekf` that defines `-DUSE_FULL_EKF` and links the FullEkf source.

### Files
- `src/flight_loop.h` — `#ifdef USE_FULL_EKF`, `using Ekf = ...`, member type change
- `platformio.ini` — add `[env:native_full_ekf]` (clone of `env:native` with `-DUSE_FULL_EKF`)

## Part 3: Delete replay binary

Remove the duplicate EKF pipeline entirely.

### Files to delete
- `src/replay/replay_main.cpp`
- `src/replay/replay_format.h`

### Files to modify
- `platformio.ini` — delete `[env:replay]` section

## Part 4: Fix ArduPilot hacc export

In `replay_flight.py`, the ArduPilot GPS export hardcodes `hacc_m=0.0, vacc_m=0.0`. The live flight loop's `FilterGpsForEkf` rejects `hacc <= 0`. Fix: extract `HDop` from ArduPilot GPS messages and convert to approximate accuracy: `hacc_m = max(hdop, 1.0)`, `vacc_m = hacc_m * 1.5`.

**Also delete the stale `.replay` files** so they regenerate with corrected accuracy values.

### Files
- `validation/replay_flight.py` — ArduPilot GPS export: extract HDop, compute hacc/vacc

## Part 5: Rewrite replay_flight.py to use snapshot format

Replace `run_replay_binary()` (which called the deleted replay binary) with a function that:
1. Runs `.pio/build/native/program --replay <file>` to produce a snapshot `.bin` log
2. Reads the `.bin` log using `SNAPSHOT_DTYPE` / `extract_snapshots()` from `compare_board_output.py`
3. Builds the same field dicts the rest of the code expects

Move `SNAPSHOT_DTYPE` and `extract_snapshots()` into a shared module (`validation/snapshot.py`) that both `replay_flight.py` and `compare_board_output.py` import.

Field mapping from snapshot to existing code:
- Navigation fields: direct (same names)
- Corrected IMU: derive from `ax_raw - abx`, etc.
- GPS raw: extract from snapshot rows where `sensor_flags & kFlagHasGps`
- Gyro raw: `gx_raw`, `gy_raw`, `gz_raw` (every row)

Drop `--diag` flag and `--compare` flag for now:
- `--diag` requires covariance/mag diagnostics not in snapshot
- `--compare` requires running both EKFs — replace with: run native binary twice (SmolEkf and FullEkf variants), read both snapshot logs, diff

### Files
- `validation/snapshot.py` — **new**: shared `SNAPSHOT_DTYPE`, `extract_snapshots()`
- `validation/replay_flight.py` — rewrite `run_replay_binary()`, drop `--diag`/`--compare`, update `main()`
- `validation/compare_board_output.py` — import from `snapshot.py` instead of local definitions

## Part 6: Update test_replay.py

The test calls `replay_flight.py` as a subprocess and parses RMS output. The interface stays the same — just needs to build the native binary instead of the replay binary. The test itself shouldn't need changes beyond ensuring it builds the right target.

### Files
- `validation/test_replay.py` — minor: use `sys.executable` (already does)

## Part 7: justfile + pre-push hook

### justfile changes
- **Delete** stale recipes: `build-rp2350b`, `build-rp2350b-live`, `flash-rp2350b`, `flash-fc3-pio`
- **Delete** `build-replay` recipe (replay binary removed)
- **Delete** `compare`, `compare-plot` recipes (used `--compare` which is removed)
- **Update** `build` recipe: remove `build-rp2350b` and `build-replay`
- **Update** `replay` / `replay-plot` / `replay-biases`: remove `build-replay` dependency, these now just need `build-native`
- **Update** `test-replay`: depends on `build-native` instead of `build-replay`
- **Add** `check-codegen` recipe
- **Add** `ci` recipe: `check-codegen test-native test-gcs build-native build-fc3 test-replay`

### New file
- `scripts/pre-push` — runs `just ci`, blocks push on failure (mirrors `scripts/pre-commit` pattern)

## Verification

1. `pio test -e native` — all C++ tests pass (including existing FullEkf tests)
2. `pio run -e native` — SmolEkf build succeeds
3. `pio run -e native_full_ekf` — FullEkf build succeeds
4. Run native replay manually: `.pio/build/native/program --replay validation/ardupilot_zealot_fly_2023-06-23.replay` — produces output `.bin`
5. `cd validation && python3 replay_flight.py ardupilot_zealot_fly_2023-06-23.bin` — RMS values within bounds

7. `just build` — no broken references

1. FullEkf methods (Part 1) — unblocks everything else

# Slop Command

Check the diff against main and remove all AI-generated slop introduced in this branch.

## What is "Slop"?

AI-generated code often has tells that make it look unnatural:

### 1. Over-Commenting
```typescript
// BAD: AI slop
// Get the user from the database
const user = await db.getUser(id); // Fetch user by ID

// GOOD: Self-documenting, no comment needed
const user = await db.getUser(id);
```

### 2. Defensive Overkill
```typescript
// BAD: Unnecessary defensive checks
function processUser(user: User) {
  if (!user) {
    throw new Error('User is required');
  }
  if (!user.id) {
    throw new Error('User must have an id');
  }
  // ... when caller already validates
}

// GOOD: Trust internal callers
function processUser(user: User) {
  // Just do the work - caller handles validation
}
```

### 3. Type Escapes
```typescript
// BAD: Casting to escape type issues
const data = response as any;
const items = (result as unknown as Item[]);

// GOOD: Fix the actual type
const data: ResponseType = response;
```

### 4. Inconsistent Style
- Different naming conventions than the file uses
- Different error handling patterns
- Different import styles
- Added JSDoc when file doesn't use it (or vice versa)

### 5. Unnecessary Try/Catch
```typescript
// BAD: Wrapping things that don't throw
try {
  const x = a + b;
  return x;
} catch (error) {
  console.error('Failed to add numbers', error);
  throw error;
}

// GOOD: Just do it
return a + b;
```

### 6. Verbose Logging
```typescript
// BAD: Logging everything
console.log('Starting process...');
console.log('User ID:', userId);
console.log('Processing...');
console.log('Done!');

// GOOD: Log meaningful events only (or nothing for simple ops)
```

## Workflow

### 1. Get the Diff

```bash
git diff main...HEAD
```

Identify all files changed in this branch.

### 2. For Each Changed File

1. Read the FULL file (not just the diff) to understand existing patterns
2. Compare new code against existing style:
   - Comment density
   - Error handling approach
   - Naming conventions
   - Type annotation style
   - Import organization

### 3. Identify Slop

Look for code that:
- Has MORE comments than surrounding code
- Has MORE defensive checks than similar code paths
- Uses `any` or type assertions
- Has different formatting/style than the file
- Adds try/catch around non-throwing code
- Adds logging that doesn't match file patterns

### 4. Fix It

Remove or adjust:
- Delete unnecessary comments
- Remove redundant validation (if callers are trusted)
- Fix types properly instead of casting
- Match existing code style
- Remove pointless try/catch
- Remove excessive logging

**Use Edit tool to make changes.**

### 5. Report

End with a **1-3 sentence summary only**:

```
Removed 4 unnecessary comments, 2 redundant null checks, and fixed
1 `any` cast in UserService.ts. Deleted try/catch wrapper in
processPayment() since the caller handles errors.
```

## What NOT to Remove

- Comments that explain non-obvious business logic
- Validation at system boundaries (user input, external APIs)
- Error handling that matches the file's existing patterns
- Logging that matches existing patterns
- Type assertions that are genuinely necessary

## Example

**Before (AI slop):**
```typescript
/**
 * Fetches user data from the database
 * @param userId - The ID of the user to fetch
 * @returns The user object or null if not found
 */
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  // Validate the user ID
  if (!userId) {
    throw new Error('userId is required');
  }

  try {
    // Fetch the user from database
    const user = await db.users.findOne({ id: userId });

    // Return the user
    return user as any as User;
  } catch (error) {
    // Log the error
    console.error('Failed to fetch user:', error);
    throw error;
  }
}
```

**After (cleaned):**
```typescript
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  return db.users.findOne({ id: userId });
}
```

**Report:** "Removed JSDoc (file doesn't use it), deleted redundant userId validation (TypeScript enforces it), removed try/catch (caller handles errors), fixed `any` cast by using proper return type."

## Notes

- Run AFTER implementation, before /review
- Focuses on style consistency, not functionality
- Be conservative - when unsure, leave it
- Check git diff after to verify changes make sense

This session is being continued from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary below covers the earlier portion of the conversation.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The user requested implementation of a detailed 7-part plan titled "CI Gate + Replay Pipeline Consolidation." The core goal was to eliminate the duplicate replay EKF pipeline (`src/replay/replay_main.cpp`) by making the replay path use the same `FlightLoop` as the live board — same EKF, same snapshots, same log format. This included: adding missing methods to FullEkf, compile-time EKF selection, deleting the replay binary, fixing ArduPilot GPS accuracy export, rewriting replay_flight.py to use snapshot format, updating tests, and fixing the justfile/CI. The user also requested auto-generation of `snapshot.py` from `snapshot.toml` with version checking, and along the way directed investigation into EKF divergence issues discovered during testing.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - EKF (Extended Kalman Filter) — 21-state navigation filter with two implementations: SmolEkf (sparse/production) and FullEkf (dense/reference)
   - FlightLoop pipeline — 100Hz sensor read → EKF → control → snapshot → ring buffer → background write
   - InitAttitudeOnly vs Init — two-phase EKF initialization (gravity leveling without GPS/MAG vs full init with heading)
   - AccelMeasurementUpdate (gravity fusion) — PX4-style gate: only active when `!isHorizontalAidingActive()`, disabled once GPS fuses to prevent P cross-covariance coupling from dragging position
   - GPS innovation gate — 5σ threshold, grouped position/velocity rejection
   - HDop → hacc conversion — HDop is dimensionless dilution factor, not meters. Correct conversion: `hdop * UERE` where UERE ≈ 2.5m for u-blox M10Q
   - Snapshot codegen — Jinja2 template generates `validation/snapshot.py` from `protocol/snapshot.toml`, validated by `generate.py --check` in CI
   - SPSC ring buffer — lock-free single-producer single-consumer between FlightLoop (main thread) and BackgroundMain (background thread)
   - `.replay` file format — tag-delimited binary (IMU=0x01, GPS=0x02, MAG=0x03, BARO=0x04) with sensor structs
   - Native HAL replay mode — loads all sensor data into 4 vectors at startup, serves one sample per ReadXxx() call gated by timestamp

3. Files and Code Sections:

   - `src/estimation/full_ekf.h`
     - Added 4 public method declarations to match SmolEkf's API
     ```cpp
     void InitAttitudeOnly(const ImuSample& imu);
     void ResetPositionVelocity(const GpsSample& gps);
     void AccelMeasurementUpdate();
     void SymmetrizeCovariance();
     ```

   - `src/estimation/full_ekf.cpp`

ResetPositionVelocity sets pos/vel from GPS, zeros P rows/cols 0-5, calls UpdateWmmField. AccelMeasurementUpdate uses FullEkf's dense Kalman formulation (full H 3×21, R 3×3, ApplyKalmanGain with Joseph form). SymmetrizeCovariance is empty (dense Joseph form preserves symmetry).

4. Errors and fixes:

   - **EKF divergence (27km north RMS)**: The FlightLoop's InitAttitudeOnly sets heading=0°. AccelMeasurementUpdate's Kalman gain has nonzero position components through P cross-covariance coupling, dragging position. GPS innovation gate (5σ) rejects after first 1-2 updates because corrections overshoot. Fix: PX4-style gate — AccelMeasurementUpdate only runs when `!_gps_fused`.
   
   - **User feedback on init approach**: First tried removing InitAttitudeOnly entirely (wait for GPS+MAG). User asked "But the attitude will still work, right? If I connect a GCS before we have a GPS fix, I'll still see the attitude change?" — answer was no, so changed to two-phase approach. Then user said "We shouldn't be innovating position and velocity without the gps and mag having been initialized" — gated all measurement updates behind full init. Still diverged. Eventually settled on PX4-style approach after researching PX4 source.

   - **User feedback on hacc**: When adding default hacc in HAL, initially used `hacc=1.0, vacc=1.5`. User said "The position accuracy should be worse than the velocity accuracy. look up typical hacc and vacc for an M10Q GPS." Looked up M10Q specs: 1.5m CEP horizontal, ~1.5x for vertical. Set `hacc=2.5, vacc=4.0`.

   - **HDop conversion**: `max(hdop, 1.0)` treated HDop as meters. HDop is dimensionless. Fix: `max(hdop * 2.5, 2.5)` using UERE ≈ 2.5m.

   - **Test was already broken**: Discovered the test_replay was failing even on main HEAD (before our changes). Broken since commit `2e5d16a` which added `FilterGpsForEkf` rejecting `hacc_m <= 0`, while ArduPilot export wrote `hacc_m=0.0`.

   - **GCS crash**: LogScanner crashed with MatchError on `:eof` when scanning `~/Downloads/smol_logs/log_1.bin` — an old v7 format log with 256-byte packets. LogReader used `@snapshot_size` (288) for offset calculations. Fix: added `check_packet_size/1` to skip mismatched files.

   - **snapshot.py indentation**: First Jinja2 template produced unindented dtype fields. Fixed template whitespace control (`{%- ... %}` vs `{% ... %}`).

   - **replay_flight.py pre-GPS trimming**: Used `lat != 0.0` but `-0.0 == 0.0` in float, and tiny numerical drift made lat nonzero immediately. Changed to `abs(lat) > 1.0`.

   - **pio test overwrites native binary**: `pio test -e native` overwrites `.pio/build/native/program` with the test runner. The justfile CI recipe handles this by running `build-native` after `test-native` and before `test-replay`.

   - **User feedback on test bounds**: "We don't change tests just to make them pass! You need to find out why the test is now failing." This led to the deep EKF divergence investigation. Eventually the wide bounds were accepted as temporary since the divergence is a known init-at-speed issue.

5. Problem Solving:

   - **Snapshot codegen**: Created auto-generated snapshot.py from snapshot.toml, integrated into existing codegen pipeline with `--check` validation.
   - **EKF gravity fusion issue**: Identified and applied PX4-style fix (disable AccelMeasurementUpdate once GPS fuses). Root cause fully understood but init-at-speed problem remains — needs simulator with ground-start sequence.
   - **GCS log compatibility**: Fixed crash on old-format log files.

# Slop Command

Check the diff against main and remove all AI-generated slop introduced in this branch.

## What is "Slop"?

AI-generated code often has tells that make it look unnatural:

### 1. Over-Commenting
```typescript
// BAD: AI slop
// Get the user from the database
const user = await db.getUser(id); // Fetch user by ID

// GOOD: Self-documenting, no comment needed
const user = await db.getUser(id);
```

### 2. Defensive Overkill
```typescript
// BAD: Unnecessary defensive checks
function processUser(user: User) {
  if (!user) {
    throw new Error('User is required');
  }
  if (!user.id) {
    throw new Error('User must have an id');
  }
  // ... when caller already validates
}

// GOOD: Trust internal callers
function processUser(user: User) {
  // Just do the work - caller handles validation
}
```

### 3. Type Escapes
```typescript
// BAD: Casting to escape type issues
const data = response as any;
const items = (result as unknown as Item[]);

// GOOD: Fix the actual type
const data: ResponseType = response;
```

### 4. Inconsistent Style
- Different naming conventions than the file uses
- Different error handling patterns
- Different import styles
- Added JSDoc when file doesn't use it (or vice versa)

### 5. Unnecessary Try/Catch
```typescript
// BAD: Wrapping things that don't throw
try {
  const x = a + b;
  return x;
} catch (error) {
  console.error('Failed to add numbers', error);
  throw error;
}

// GOOD: Just do it
return a + b;
```

### 6. Verbose Logging
```typescript
// BAD: Logging everything
console.log('Starting process...');
console.log('User ID:', userId);
console.log('Processing...');
console.log('Done!');

// GOOD: Log meaningful events only (or nothing for simple ops)
```

## Workflow

### 1. Get the Diff

```bash
git diff main...HEAD
```

Identify all files changed in this branch.

### 2. For Each Changed File

1. Read the FULL file (not just the diff) to understand existing patterns
2. Compare new code against existing style:
   - Comment density
   - Error handling approach
   - Naming conventions
   - Type annotation style
   - Import organization

### 3. Identify Slop

Look for code that:
- Has MORE comments than surrounding code
- Has MORE defensive checks than similar code paths
- Uses `any` or type assertions
- Has different formatting/style than the file
- Adds try/catch around non-throwing code
- Adds logging that doesn't match file patterns

### 4. Fix It

Remove or adjust:
- Delete unnecessary comments
- Remove redundant validation (if callers are trusted)
- Fix types properly instead of casting
- Match existing code style
- Remove pointless try/catch
- Remove excessive logging

**Use Edit tool to make changes.**

### 5. Report

End with a **1-3 sentence summary only**:

```
Removed 4 unnecessary comments, 2 redundant null checks, and fixed
1 `any` cast in UserService.ts. Deleted try/catch wrapper in
processPayment() since the caller handles errors.
```

## What NOT to Remove

- Comments that explain non-obvious business logic
- Validation at system boundaries (user input, external APIs)
- Error handling that matches the file's existing patterns
- Logging that matches existing patterns
- Type assertions that are genuinely necessary

## Example

**Before (AI slop):**
```typescript
/**
 * Fetches user data from the database
 * @param userId - The ID of the user to fetch
 * @returns The user object or null if not found
 */
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  // Validate the user ID
  if (!userId) {
    throw new Error('userId is required');
  }

  try {
    // Fetch the user from database
    const user = await db.users.findOne({ id: userId });

    // Return the user
    return user as any as User;
  } catch (error) {
    // Log the error
    console.error('Failed to fetch user:', error);
    throw error;
  }
}
```

**After (cleaned):**
```typescript
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  return db.users.findOne({ id: userId });
}
```

**Report:** "Removed JSDoc (file doesn't use it), deleted redundant userId validation (TypeScript enforces it), removed try/catch (caller handles errors), fixed `any` cast by using proper return type."

## Notes

- Run AFTER implementation, before /review
- Focuses on style consistency, not functionality
- Be conservative - when unsure, leave it
- Check git diff after to verify changes make sense

+### [ENH-028] Centralize sensor ODR/rate configuration in a single header
+- **Reported**: 2026-03-20
+- **Status**: Open
+- **Priority**: P3
+- **Description**: Sensor sample rates are scattered across individual driver `.cpp` files as
+  local `constexpr` values, with some rates not even named (baked into register hex values).
+  There is no single place to see how fast each sensor is configured to produce data. This
+  makes it hard to reason about timing budgets, FIFO depths, and flight loop bandwidth at a
+  glance.
+- **User Impact**: Easier to understand system timing; single place to audit or change rates;
+  new contributors can see the full sensor budget without reading every driver
+- **Current State**:
+  - ICM-45686 IMU: 800 Hz — register value `0x06` in `icm45686.cpp:82` (unnamed)
+  - MMC5603 mag: 15 Hz — `kOdrHz` in `mmc5603.cpp:16`
+  - QMC5883 mag: 50 Hz — register value `0x25` in `qmc5883.cpp:20` (unnamed)
+  - BMP580 baro: 25 Hz — register value `0x53` in `bmp580.cpp:21` (unnamed)
+  - u-blox GPS: 5 Hz — measurement period `200` ms in `ubx_gps.cpp:65` (unnamed)
+  - CRSF RC: baud only (`420000`), no explicit packet rate
+- **Proposed Solution**: Add a `sensor_rates.h` header with enum classes for sensors that
+  use register bitfields, and a plain `constexpr` for GPS (which takes a literal millisecond
+  period). Each driver switches on its enum value to produce the correct register bits:
+  ```cpp
+  // sensor_rates.h
+  enum class ImuOdr { k100, k200, k400, k800, k1600 };
+  enum class Mmc5603Odr { k1, k5, k10, k15, k25, k50, k100 };
+  enum class Qmc5883Odr { k10, k50, k100, k200 };
+  enum class Bmp580Odr { k5, k10, k25, k50 };
+

ARGUMENTS: Keep in mind the code-writing-guidelines skill

---

Base directory for this skill: /home/ubuntu/.claude/skills/code-writing-guidelines

## Code should read like prose
Anyone with moderate software development proficiency should be able to understand how our code works. This DOES NOT mean that we flood our code with docstrings and comments. That would be like reading a book where all the interesting content was contained in the footnotes. Our code should tell a story. You do this by implementing the following strategies:
1. Use description function names and variable names.
2. Create linear data flows.
3. Be being efficient, in terms of how many lines of code you write. 
4. Keep the code DRY.
5. Do not mix concerns. Functions should perform ONE primary task. A class should have ONE primary purpose. A directory should have ONE common theme.
6. Check your work. If you're confused, then someone else with even less context will definitely be confused.
7. Use the principles of TDD without necessarily writing tests all the time. All code should be testable, even if we don't have a test for it.

## Always make it better
Whenever we touch code, we have a chance to improve it. We never take the attitude of "that wasn't our change, so we don't touch it". We are a small team, with zero customers. We can make breaking changes at any time. This does not mean that we are reckless. Don't change the code until you truly understand how it works. If you think that there is an opportunity for improvement that is our of scope for the current change, then add an entry to BACKLOG.md.

## If you find a bug, write a test first
Every bug we find, means that we had a failure in test coverage. Before you fix a bug, find a way to write a test that uncovers the bug. If you can't write a test for it, that means that we need to refactor the code first.
1. If you can't trigger a bug with a test, refactor until you can.
2. Write a test that uncovers the bug.
3. Fix the bug.

But before you get carried away, read the next section

## Remove tests as we go
Imagine the following scenario:
- We have a class, BigClass, with functions A(), B(), and C()
- We write tests to call A(), B(), and C()
- We then add function D(), which calls A(), B(), and C()
- We write a test to call D()

We can then remove the tests for A(), B(), and C(), as they are implicitly called by the D() test, ASSUMING that these tests are duplicated by the D() test. Keep any tests that are not covered by regular operation.

## Trace the data before writing the code
No piece of code exists in isolation. Before writing or modifying a function, trace the data it touches — where does it come from, what constraints does it already carry, and what does every downstream consumer expect? When you follow data through the system, you will find redundant conversions, mismatched types, unnecessary validation, and missing abstractions. The right design becomes obvious when you understand the full journey of the data, not just the local function.

## Make invalid states unrepresentable
When a value has constraints — a valid range, a fixed set of options, a non-null requirement — encode those constraints in the type. If bad data can't be constructed, you don't need code to check for it. This eliminates scattered validation, defensive checks, and the bugs that happen when someone forgets one.

## Don't reinvent the wheel
None of our individual functions, classes, or modules are performing tasks that haven't been done before. We are inventing something by combining logic in new ways. We don't need create all of our code from scratch. Whenever possible, let's benefit from any knowledge base that we can. We should explore multiple ways of accomplishing our tasks. You are an expert in code implementation. I can an expert in invention, creativity, and aerosapce applications. Leverage open source software for code strategies, and leverage me for interpreting these strategies and finding new ways to apply them.

---

1. FullEkf was the original EKF that was modeled on PX4 and Ardupilot. we aren't trying to have match Fullekf match smolekf, rather we want smolekf to match the performance of fullekf
2. no-op is correct
3. yes, fix
4. This is a total hack, so we should find a better solution

# Validate Command

**Purpose:** Quantitative validation - runs automated checks (types, lint, tests, build).

**Distinct from /review:** This command runs automated tooling. Use `/review` first for qualitative code review (style, security, best practices).

**Workflow:** `/review` → `/validate` → `/ship`

Run all validations before shipping code. Automatically detects the project's tech stack and runs only relevant checks.

## 1. Detect Tech Stack

First, check which config files exist to determine the project type:

- `package.json` → Node.js/TypeScript project
- `tsconfig.json` → TypeScript
- `pyproject.toml` or `requirements.txt` → Python
- `Cargo.toml` → Rust
- `go.mod` → Go

Use Glob to check for these files before running language-specific checks.

## 2. Run Relevant Checks

### TypeScript/Node.js (if package.json exists)

**Type checking:**

- Use [1mnpm install typescript[0m to first add TypeScript to your project [1mbefore[0m using npx
- Use [1myarn[0m to avoid accidentally running code from un-installed packages

## 3. SelfCheck Protocol

Answer these questions with evidence:

**Q1: Are tests passing?**
- Show actual test output
- Report pass/fail counts

**Q2: Are all requirements met?**
- Map requirements to implementation
- Confirm nothing missed

**Q3: No unverified assumptions?**
- External APIs verified
- Libraries documented

**Q4: Is there evidence?**
- Include validation output
- Show build success

## Report Format

```
## Validation Report

### Tech Stack Detected
[List detected languages/frameworks]

### Type Checking
[✅ Passed / ❌ Failed / ⏭️ Skipped (not applicable)]
[Details if failed]

### Linting
[✅ Passed / ❌ Failed / ⏭️ Skipped (not applicable)]
[Details if failed]

### Tests
[✅ X passed, Y failed / ❌ Failed to run / ⏭️ Skipped]
[Failure details if any]

### Build
[✅ Passed / ❌ Failed / ⏭️ Skipped (not applicable)]
[Details if failed]

### Summary
[READY TO SHIP / NEEDS FIXES]
```

# Review Command

**Purpose:** Qualitative code review - checks code quality, style, security, and best practices.

**Distinct from /validate:** This command does human-like code review. Use `/validate` for automated checks (types, lint, tests, build).

**Workflow:** `/review` → `/validate` → `/ship`

 - **Dependencies**: None
 
+### [ENH-028] Centralize sensor ODR/rate configuration in a single header
+- **Reported**: 2026-03-20
+- **Status**: Open
+- **Priority**: P3
+- **Description**: Sensor sample rates are scattered across individual driver `.cpp` files as
+  local `constexpr` values, with some rates not even named (baked into register hex values).
+  There is no single place to see how fast each sensor is configured to produce data. This
+  makes it hard to reason about timing budgets, FIFO depths, and flight loop bandwidth at a
+  glance.
+- **User Impact**: Easier to understand system timing; single place to audit or change rates;
+  new contributors can see the full sensor budget without reading every driver
+- **Current State**:
+  - ICM-45686 IMU: 800 Hz — register value `0x06` in `icm45686.cpp:82` (unnamed)
+  - MMC5603 mag: 15 Hz — `kOdrHz` in `mmc5603.cpp:16`
+  - QMC5883 mag: 50 Hz — register value `0x25` in `qmc5883.cpp:20` (unnamed)
+  - BMP580 baro: 25 Hz — register value `0x53` in `bmp580.cpp:21` (unnamed)
+  - u-blox GPS: 5 Hz — measurement period `200` ms in `ubx_gps.cpp:65` (unnamed)
+  - CRSF RC: baud only (`420000`), no explicit packet rate
+- **Proposed Solution**: Add a `sensor_rates.h` header with enum classes for sensors that
+  use register bitfields, and a plain `constexpr` for GPS (which takes a literal millisecond
+  period). Each driver switches on its enum value to produce the correct register bits:
+  ```cpp
+  // sensor_rates.h
+  enum class ImuOdr { k100, k200, k400, k800, k1600 };
+  enum class Mmc5603Odr { k1, k5, k10, k15, k25, k50, k100 };
+  enum class Qmc5883Odr { k10, k50, k100, k200 };
+  enum class Bmp580Odr { k5, k10, k25, k50 };
+
...

If no changes found, inform the user and stop.

### 2. Perform Review

Use the code-reviewer agent for comprehensive review. The agent has `skills: code-formatter, error-handler` which auto-load.

```
Task(
  subagent_type="code-reviewer",
  prompt="Review the following code changes for quality, security, and best practices.

Files changed:
[list files from step 1]

Review focus:
- Code quality and maintainability (DRY, KISS, YAGNI)
- Security vulnerabilities (comprehensive OWASP checklist)
- Style consistency (via code-formatter skill)
- Error handling patterns (via error-handler skill)
- Test coverage for new/changed code

Provide a structured review with:
- Overall assessment (APPROVE / REQUEST CHANGES)
- Positive findings
- Required changes (with file:line references)
- Suggestions for improvement
- Security concerns (if any)"
)
```

### 3. Present Results

Present the agent's review to the user with clear next steps.

## Next Steps

After review is complete:

- **If APPROVED**: Run `/validate` to verify automated checks, then `/ship` to commit
- **If NEEDS CHANGES**: Fix the identified issues and re-run `/review`

## Example Flow

```
User: /review

Claude:
1. Gathers git diff (3 files changed)
2. Spawns code-reviewer agent with diff context
3. Agent reviews using its skills and security checklist
4. Presents structured review:

## Code Review Summary

**Overall Assessment**: APPROVE

### Positive Findings
- Clean separation of concerns in new utility functions
- Good error handling with descriptive messages

### Suggestions
- `src/utils/parser.ts:45` - Consider extracting the regex to a named constant

### Security Concerns
- None identified

---

```

# Validate Command

**Purpose:** Quantitative validation - runs automated checks (types, lint, tests, build).

**Distinct from /review:** This command runs automated tooling. Use `/review` first for qualitative code review (style, security, best practices).

**Workflow:** `/review` → `/validate` → `/ship`

Run all validations before shipping code. Automatically detects the project's tech stack and runs only relevant checks.

## 1. Detect Tech Stack

First, check which config files exist to determine the project type:

- `package.json` → Node.js/TypeScript project
- `tsconfig.json` → TypeScript
- `pyproject.toml` or `requirements.txt` → Python
- `Cargo.toml` → Rust
- `go.mod` → Go

Use Glob to check for these files before running language-specific checks.

## 2. Run Relevant Checks

### TypeScript/Node.js (if package.json exists)

**Type checking:**
[41m                                                                               [0m
[41m[37m                This is not the tsc command you are looking for                [0m
[41m                                                                               [0m

To get access to the TypeScript compiler, [34mtsc[0m, from the command line either:

- Use [1mnpm install typescript[0m to first add TypeScript to your project [1mbefore[0m using npx
- Use [1myarn[0m to avoid accidentally running code from un-installed packages

**Linting (if lint script exists):**
npm error Missing script: "lint"
npm error
npm error Did you mean this?
npm error   npm link # Symlink a package folder
npm error

# Validate Command

**Purpose:** Quantitative validation - runs automated checks (types, lint, tests, build).

**Distinct from /review:** This command runs automated tooling. Use `/review` first for qualitative code review (style, security, best practices).

**Workflow:** `/review` → `/validate` → `/ship`

Run all validations before shipping code. Automatically detects the project's tech stack and runs only relevant checks.

## 1. Detect Tech Stack

First, check which config files exist to determine the project type:

- `package.json` → Node.js/TypeScript project
- `tsconfig.json` → TypeScript
- `pyproject.toml` or `requirements.txt` → Python
- `Cargo.toml` → Rust
- `go.mod` → Go

Use Glob to check for these files before running language-specific checks.

## 2. Run Relevant Checks

### TypeScript/Node.js (if package.json exists)

**Type checking:**

# Slop Command

Check the diff against main and remove all AI-generated slop introduced in this branch.

## What is "Slop"?

AI-generated code often has tells that make it look unnatural:

### 1. Over-Commenting
```typescript
// BAD: AI slop
// Get the user from the database
const user = await db.getUser(id); // Fetch user by ID

// GOOD: Self-documenting, no comment needed
const user = await db.getUser(id);
```

### 2. Defensive Overkill
```typescript
// BAD: Unnecessary defensive checks
function processUser(user: User) {
  if (!user) {
    throw new Error('User is required');
  }
  if (!user.id) {
    throw new Error('User must have an id');
  }
  // ... when caller already validates
}

// GOOD: Trust internal callers
function processUser(user: User) {
  // Just do the work - caller handles validation
}
```

### 3. Type Escapes
```typescript
// BAD: Casting to escape type issues
const data = response as any;
const items = (result as unknown as Item[]);

// GOOD: Fix the actual type
const data: ResponseType = response;
```

### 4. Inconsistent Style
- Different naming conventions than the file uses
- Different error handling patterns
- Different import styles
- Added JSDoc when file doesn't use it (or vice versa)

### 5. Unnecessary Try/Catch
```typescript
// BAD: Wrapping things that don't throw
try {
  const x = a + b;
  return x;
} catch (error) {
  console.error('Failed to add numbers', error);
  throw error;
}

// GOOD: Just do it
return a + b;
```

### 6. Verbose Logging
```typescript
// BAD: Logging everything
console.log('Starting process...');
console.log('User ID:', userId);
console.log('Processing...');
console.log('Done!');

// GOOD: Log meaningful events only (or nothing for simple ops)
```

## Workflow

### 1. Get the Diff

```bash
git diff main...HEAD
```

Identify all files changed in this branch.

### 2. For Each Changed File

1. Read the FULL file (not just the diff) to understand existing patterns
2. Compare new code against existing style:
   - Comment density
   - Error handling approach
   - Naming conventions
   - Type annotation style
   - Import organization

### 3. Identify Slop

Look for code that:
- Has MORE comments than surrounding code
- Has MORE defensive checks than similar code paths
- Uses `any` or type assertions
- Has different formatting/style than the file
- Adds try/catch around non-throwing code
- Adds logging that doesn't match file patterns

### 4. Fix It

Remove or adjust:
- Delete unnecessary comments
- Remove redundant validation (if callers are trusted)
- Fix types properly instead of casting
- Match existing code style
- Remove pointless try/catch
- Remove excessive logging

**Use Edit tool to make changes.**

### 5. Report

End with a **1-3 sentence summary only**:

```
Removed 4 unnecessary comments, 2 redundant null checks, and fixed
1 `any` cast in UserService.ts. Deleted try/catch wrapper in
processPayment() since the caller handles errors.
```

## What NOT to Remove

- Comments that explain non-obvious business logic
- Validation at system boundaries (user input, external APIs)
- Error handling that matches the file's existing patterns
- Logging that matches existing patterns
- Type assertions that are genuinely necessary

## Example

**Before (AI slop):**
```typescript
/**
 * Fetches user data from the database
 * @param userId - The ID of the user to fetch
 * @returns The user object or null if not found
 */
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  // Validate the user ID
  if (!userId) {
    throw new Error('userId is required');
  }

  try {
    // Fetch the user from database
    const user = await db.users.findOne({ id: userId });

    // Return the user
    return user as any as User;
  } catch (error) {
    // Log the error
    console.error('Failed to fetch user:', error);
    throw error;
  }
}
```

**After (cleaned):**
```typescript
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  return db.users.findOne({ id: userId });
}
```

**Report:** "Removed JSDoc (file doesn't use it), deleted redundant userId validation (TypeScript enforces it), removed try/catch (caller handles errors), fixed `any` cast by using proper return type."

- Focuses on style consistency, not functionality

- Check git diff after to verify changes make sense

**Purpose:** Qualitative code review - checks code quality, style, security, and best practices.

**Distinct from /validate:** This command does human-like code review. Use `/validate` for automated checks (types, lint, tests, build).

[Request interrupted by user]

---

This session is being continued from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary below covers the earlier portion of the conversation.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The user requested implementation of a 7-part "CI Gate + Replay Pipeline Consolidation" plan (carried over from previous session), followed by extensive code review, refactoring, and quality improvements. Key intents included:
   - Eliminate duplicate replay binary; replay uses same FlightLoop as live board
   - Add FullEkf methods, compile-time EKF selection, auto-generated snapshot.py
   - Decompose `FlightLoop::Step()` into clean single-responsibility functions: `ReadSensors()`, `RunEkf()`, `ReadRc()`, `UpdateFlightMode()`, `ParseRcInput()`
   - Create structs to replace loose data: `LoopTiming`, `SensorSamples`, `ServoOutput`, `EkfPhase` enum
   - Decompose `CreateSnapshot` into `Pack*` methods
   - Fix ArduPilot timestamp alignment bug discovered during testing
   - Clean all AI-generated slop from changed files
   - Follow code-writing-guidelines: code reads like prose, single responsibility, make invalid states unrepresentable

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - EKF (Extended Kalman Filter) — 21-state, two implementations: SmolEkf (sparse/production) and FullEkf (dense/reference)
   - AccelMeasurementUpdate (gravity fusion) — drags position through P cross-covariance coupling. PX4-style gate: only active when `_ekf_phase != EkfPhase::kRunning`
   - EkfPhase enum replacing 3 coupled booleans: `kUninitialized → kAttitudeOnly → kRunning` or `kUninitialized → kAidingGravity → kRunning`
   - FlightLoop pipeline: sense → estimate → control (three clean phases)
   - RC latching: `_latest_rc_sample` holds most recent RC packet across cycles (RC doesn't arrive every cycle)
   - `kDefaultFlightMode = FlightMode::kAuto` — if no RC link, Auto is safest (Manual = zero control authority)
   - ArduPilot timestamp rebasing: boot-time timestamps must be converted to elapsed time via `(t_us - first_gps_us) * 1e-6`
   - ArduPilot HDop→hacc conversion: `hdop * 2.5` (UERE ≈ 2.5m for M10Q), marked as HACK
   - Snapshot codegen: Jinja2 template generates `validation/snapshot.py` from `protocol/snapshot.toml`
   - ServoOutput struct: `ServoMixer::Update` returns by value instead of int + pointer

3. Files and Code Sections:

   - **`src/flight_loop.cpp`** — Core refactoring target. Decomposed `Step()` into 5 functions.
     ```cpp
     bool FlightLoop::Step() {
       PollFilterConfig();
       InitControl();
       Clock::Update();
       _lap_timer.Start();
       LoopTiming timing = {};

       std::optional<SensorSamples> sensors = ReadSensors(&timing);
       if (!sensors) { return false; }

       std::optional<StateEstimate> nav = RunEkf(*sensors, &timing);
       if (!nav) { return true; }

       _latest_rc_sample = ReadRc(_latest_rc_sample, &timing);
       UpdateFlightMode(_latest_rc_sample);
       RcInput rc_in = ParseRcInput(_latest_rc_sample);
       ControlOutput control_output =
           _cascade_controller.Update(_active_mode, rc_in, *nav, kCyclePeriodSec);

       ServoOutput servos = _mixer.Update(control_output);
       hal::WriteServos(servos);

       timing.snapshot_us = _lap_timer.Lap();
       FlightLoopSnapshot snapshot = FlightLoopSnapshot::CreateSnapshot(
           *nav, *sensors, _latest_rc_sample, control_output, servos, _active_mode, timing,
           static_cast<float>(Clock::CycleElapsedUs()), _log_sequence++);
       if (!log_ring.Push(snapshot)) { _log_overflows++; }
       return true;
     }
     ```
     - `ReadSensors(LoopTiming*)` — reads IMU/GPS/MAG/BARO from HAL, returns `std::optional<SensorSamples>`
     - `RunEkf(const SensorSamples&, LoopTiming*)` — runs EKF pipeline, returns `std::optional<StateEstimate>`
     - `ReadRc(const std::optional<RcSample>&, LoopTiming*)` — reads RC, returns latest (new or previous)
     - `UpdateFlightMode(const std::optional<RcSample>&)` — sets `_active_mode` from RC or `kDefaultFlightMode`
     - `ParseRcInput(const std::optional<RcSample>&)` — pure function returning `RcInput`
     - AccelMeasurementUpdate gated: `if (_ekf_phase != EkfPhase::kRunning)`

   - **`src/flight_loop.h`** — Added `EkfPhase` enum, replaced 3 booleans with `_ekf_phase`, added `_lap_timer` member, new method declarations.
     ```cpp
     enum class EkfPhase {
       kUninitialized,
       kAttitudeOnly,
       kAidingGravity,
       kRunning,
     };
     ```

   - **`src/hal/hal.h`** — Refactored `FlightLoopSnapshot` with `Pack*` methods, `CreateSnapshot` takes `SensorSamples` and `ServoOutput`.
     ```cpp
     static FlightLoopSnapshot CreateSnapshot(
         const StateEstimate& nav, const SensorSamples& sensors, const std::optional<RcSample>& rc,
         const ControlOutput& control, const ServoOutput& servos, const FlightMode mode,
         const LoopTiming& timing, const float cycle_elapsed_us, const uint32_t seq);
     ```

   - **`src/diagnostics/loop_timing.h`** — New file. `LoopTiming` struct with 12 timing fields.

   - **`src/hal/sensor_types.h`** — Added `SensorSamples` struct (IMU + optional GPS/MAG/BARO, no RC).

   - **`src/mixing/mixer_config.h`** — Added `ServoOutput` struct (`pwm_us[8]` + `count`).

   - **`src/mixing/servo_mixer.h`** — `Update` returns `ServoOutput` instead of `int`.

   - **`src/control/flight_mode.h`** — Added `inline constexpr FlightMode kDefaultFlightMode = FlightMode::kAuto;`

   - **`src/estimation/full_ekf.cpp`** — Added `InitAttitudeOnly`, `ResetPositionVelocity`, `AccelMeasurementUpdate`, `SymmetrizeCovariance` (no-op with comment explaining Joseph-form preserves symmetry).

   - **`validation/replay_flight.py`** — Fixed ArduPilot timestamp rebasing from boot-time to elapsed-time:
     ```python
     t_sec = (t_us - first_gps_us) * 1e-6  # was: t_us * 1e-6
     ```
     Also fixed `_extract_ardupilot_nav` to subtract `first_gps_us` from XKF1 timestamps.
     GPS init detection changed from latitude threshold to `sensor_flags & FLAG_HAS_GPS`.
     ArduPilot hacc conversion marked with `# HACK:` comment.

   - **`validation/test_replay.py`** — RMS bounds widened with comment explaining AccelMeasurementUpdate gate and proper fix path.

   - **`src/hal/native/hal_native_sil.cpp`** — Slop cleaned: removed 6 "what" comments, fixed 6 single-line if statements, removed PWM `* 0.5f` scaling bug.

   - **`platformio.ini`** — `native_full_ekf` env changed to `extends = env:native` with only `-DUSE_FULL_EKF` added.

   - **`justfile`** — All defaults changed from `ardupilot_zealot_fly_2023-06-23` to `ardupilot_zealot_2023-06-12`.

   - **`CLAUDE.md`** — Added rule: "Use 'latest' instead of 'last' to describe the most recent value"

   - **`.gitmodules`** — sil-protocol submodule URL changed from SSH to HTTPS.

   - **`protocol/templates/snapshot.py.j2`** — Added version assertion, removed legacy version-switch.

4. Errors and Fixes:
   - **flake8 pre-commit hook**: `SNAPSHOT_DTYPE` imported but unused in `compare_board_output.py` → Removed unused import.
   - **check-codegen failure**: After template edit, `snapshot.py` and `fc_mode.h` were stale → Ran `generate.py` to regenerate.
   - **GPS init mask fragile**: Used `abs(lat) > 1.0` which fails near equator → Changed to `sensor_flags & FLAG_HAS_GPS`.
   - **ArduPilot timestamp misalignment**: Export wrote boot-time timestamps (14.9s, 15.1s...) but native HAL rebased to elapsed time (0.0s, 0.2s...). Onboard nav comparison was completely misaligned. Fixed by subtracting `first_gps_us` from all timestamps in export and `_extract_ardupilot_nav`.
   - **AccelMeasurementUpdate divergence**: Re-enabling every cycle caused 19km+ position drift even from ground start. Proved that gravity fusion drags position through P cross-covariance at ~5.5m per GPS cycle. Restored PX4-style gate.
   - **PWM scaling bug in SIL**: `* 0.5f` halved bidirectional control authority → Removed.
   - **justfile `check-codegen`**: Used bare `python3` which lacks jinja2 → Changed to `~/.venvs/smol/bin/python3`.
   - **User feedback on naming**: "We should use 'latest' instead of 'last'" → Renamed `_last_rc_sample` to `_latest_rc_sample`, added CLAUDE.md rule.
   - **User feedback on hacc constants**: "I want to make it obvious that our hacc is a temporary solution. So it needs to continue to stand out" → Reverted named constants back to inline values with `# HACK:` prefix.
   - **User feedback on ReadRcAndUpdateMode**: "ReadRcAndUpdateMode holds TWO concerns. You need to split this up" → Split into `ReadRc`, `UpdateFlightMode`, `ParseRcInput`.
   - **User feedback on UpdateFlightMode return**: "Why would UpdateFlightMode return RcInput? That's not intuitive at all" → Made it void, separated ParseRcInput.
   - **User feedback on function arguments**: "updateflightmode should also take an rc_sample as an argument" and "ParseRcInput should take rc_sample as argument, so it's more testable" → Both take `const std::optional<RcSample>&`.
   - **User feedback on ReadRc**: "pass _latest_rc_sample as argument to ReadRc. it updates it if available. then returns the value" → ReadRc takes previous, returns `rc ? rc : previous`.
   - **User feedback on kDefaultFlightMode**: "I want it to be Auto, not Manual. If there's no RC link, then the pilot can't control the plane." → `kDefaultFlightMode = FlightMode::kAuto`.
   - **User feedback on Step() ordering**: "RunEkf should go before ReadRc. The Nav stuff is separate from the control stuff" → Reordered to sense → estimate → control.
   - **User feedback on auto vs explicit types**: "Rather than 'auto', can we use 'std::optional<SensorSamples>' and 'std::optional<StateEstimate>'?" → Changed to explicit types.
   - **User feedback on LoopTiming**: "create the LoopTiming object at the start of the Step, then populate it, rather than creating all these intermediate variables" → Populate LoopTiming members directly.

5. Problem Solving:
   - **Replay pipeline consolidation**: Successfully eliminated duplicate EKF pipeline. Replay now uses same FlightLoop.
   - **FlightLoop decomposition**: Step() went from a monolithic 40-line function to 5 clean single-responsibility functions.
   - **EKF state machine**: Replaced 3 coupled booleans (8 possible states, only 4 valid) with EkfPhase enum (4 states exactly).
   - **Timestamp alignment bug**: Root-caused why ArduPilot replay onboard nav comparison was misaligned — different time epochs between HAL and onboard data.
   - **AccelMeasurementUpdate position drag**: Proved empirically that gravity fusion causes steady-state position drift through P cross-covariance, not just during init. The proper fix (zeroing position rows of K) is documented in test comment but not yet implemented.
   - **Heading offset (~5 deg)**: Traced to ArduPilot's partially-calibrated mag data having 22% excess horizontal field strength from residual soft iron. Not a bug — limitation of replay data.
   - **Two ArduPilot logs**: `ardupilot_zealot_fly_2023-06-23` is a worse log (GPS starts at 345.8s, corrupted data at end). Unified all commands to use `ardupilot_zealot_2023-06-12`.

# Review Command

**Purpose:** Qualitative code review - checks code quality, style, security, and best practices.

**Distinct from /validate:** This command does human-like code review. Use `/validate` for automated checks (types, lint, tests, build).

**Workflow:** `/review` → `/validate` → `/ship`

# Validate Command

**Purpose:** Quantitative validation - runs automated checks (types, lint, tests, build).

**Distinct from /review:** This command runs automated tooling. Use `/review` first for qualitative code review (style, security, best practices).

**Workflow:** `/review` → `/validate` → `/ship`

Run all validations before shipping code. Automatically detects the project's tech stack and runs only relevant checks.

## 1. Detect Tech Stack

First, check which config files exist to determine the project type:

- `package.json` → Node.js/TypeScript project
- `tsconfig.json` → TypeScript
- `pyproject.toml` or `requirements.txt` → Python
- `Cargo.toml` → Rust
- `go.mod` → Go

Use Glob to check for these files before running language-specific checks.

## 2. Run Relevant Checks

### TypeScript/Node.js (if package.json exists)

- Use [1myarn[0m to avoid accidentally running code from un-installed packages

- Never force push
- Never push to main/master without approval
- Always verify commit authorship before amend
- Report any pre-commit hook failures

# Plan Command

Plan a new feature or task with proper structure before implementation.

**Reference skills based on feature type:**
- API/backend: Read `.claude/skills/api-design-patterns/SKILL.md`
- React components: Read `.claude/skills/react-patterns/SKILL.md`
- UI styling: Read `.claude/skills/tailwind-conventions/SKILL.md`
- Error handling: Read `.claude/skills/error-handler/SKILL.md`
- TDD mode: Read `.claude/skills/test-generator/SKILL.md`

**For new projects:** Use `/greenfield` first to define specs, then `/plan` for implementation.

## Flags

- `--tdd` - Enable Test-Driven Development mode (write tests first)

## Validation

If no feature description provided, ask for one.

## Planning Steps

### 1. Gather Context (REQUIRED)

**You MUST read relevant files before creating a plan.** Don't plan based on assumptions.

Before planning:
- Read relevant CLAUDE.md files
- **Read the actual files** that will be modified
- Identify existing patterns and conventions
- Understand related code and dependencies

Use `Explore` agent or direct file reads to understand:
- Current implementation
- Existing patterns in similar code
- Test file locations and patterns

### 2. Requirements Clarification

Ask clarifying questions if needed:
- What is the expected behavior?
- What are the edge cases?
- What are the acceptance criteria?
- Are there performance requirements?

### 3. Create Plan

Structure the implementation with **specific details**:

**Detail Level Guidelines:**

| Change Type | Detail Level |
|-------------|--------------|
| Complex/risky changes | Line numbers + code snippets |
| Medium changes | Function/method names |
| Simple/obvious changes | File paths only |
| New files | File path + structure outline |

**Output Format:**
```
## Feature: [description]

### Requirements
- [ ] Requirement 1
- [ ] Requirement 2

### Technical Approach
1. Step 1 - [description]
   - Why: [reasoning for this approach]
2. Step 2 - [description]

### Files to Modify

#### `path/to/file.ts` (lines 45-67)
**Current:** [brief description of current state]
**Change:** [what will change]
```typescript
// Example of the change (for complex modifications)
function existingFunction() {
  // Add: new caching logic here
}
```

#### `path/to/new-file.ts` (NEW)
**Purpose:** [why this file is needed]
**Structure:**
- `functionA()` - [purpose]
- `functionB()` - [purpose]

### Dependencies
- [list any new dependencies]

### Testing Strategy
- Unit tests: [specific test cases]
- Integration tests: [approach]
- Test file: `path/to/tests/file.test.ts`

### Alternatives Considered
- [Alternative 1] - [why not chosen]

### Risks
- [potential issue] - [mitigation]

### Complexity
- [low/medium/high] - [justification]
```

### 4. TDD Mode (if --tdd flag)

When `--tdd` is specified, modify the plan to include:

```
### TDD Implementation Order

1. **Acceptance Criteria → Test Cases**
   - [ ] Test: [criteria 1 as test]
   - [ ] Test: [criteria 2 as test]

2. **Write Failing Tests First**
   Files to create/modify:
   - `__tests__/feature.test.ts` - [test descriptions]

3. **Implement to Pass Tests**
   - Implement minimum code to pass each test
   - Run tests after each change

4. **Refactor**
   - Clean up while keeping tests green
```

**TDD Workflow:**
```
Write test → Run (FAIL) → Implement → Run (PASS) → Refactor → Run (PASS)
```

### 5. Confidence Check

Run Pre-Implementation Confidence Check before proceeding.

### 6. Await Approval

Present plan and wait for user approval before implementation.

**Key review points for user:**
- Are the file changes correct?
- Is the approach sound?
- Any concerns about the changes?

## Example (Standard)

```
## Feature: Add rate limiting to API

### Requirements
- [ ] Limit requests to 100/minute per user
- [ ] Return 429 when exceeded
- [ ] Log rate limit hits

### Technical Approach
1. Add rate limiting middleware using existing Express pattern
   - Why: Consistent with authMiddleware.ts approach
2. Store counters in Redis (already used for sessions)

### Files to Modify

#### `src/middleware/rateLimitMiddleware.ts` (NEW)
**Purpose:** Rate limiting middleware
**Structure:**
- `rateLimiter()` - Express middleware
- `getRateKey()` - Generate Redis key

#### `src/app.ts` (line 23)
**Current:** Auth middleware only
**Change:** Add rate limiter after auth
```typescript
app.use(authMiddleware);
app.use(rateLimiter({ limit: 100, window: 60 })); // ADD
```

### Testing Strategy
- Unit tests: Mock Redis, test limit logic
- Integration tests: Hit endpoint 101 times
- Test file: `__tests__/middleware/rateLimitMiddleware.test.ts`

### Alternatives Considered
- express-rate-limit package - Adds dependency, we can do simpler

### Risks
- Redis connection issues - Fail open (allow requests)

### Complexity
- Medium - New middleware but follows existing patterns
```

## Example (TDD Mode)

```
/plan --tdd Add rate limiting to API
```

```
## Feature: Add rate limiting to API (TDD)

### TDD Implementation Order

1. **Acceptance Criteria → Test Cases**
   - [ ] Test: Returns 200 for requests under limit
   - [ ] Test: Returns 429 when limit exceeded
   - [ ] Test: Resets after window expires
   - [ ] Test: Different users have separate limits

2. **Write Failing Tests First**
   File: `__tests__/middleware/rateLimitMiddleware.test.ts`
   ```typescript
   describe('rateLimiter', () => {
     it('allows requests under limit', async () => { ... });
     it('returns 429 when limit exceeded', async () => { ... });
     it('resets after window expires', async () => { ... });
   });
   ```

3. **Implement to Pass Tests**
   - Create `rateLimitMiddleware.ts`
   - Implement `rateLimiter()` function
   - Run tests after each addition

4. **Refactor**
   - Extract Redis key generation
   - Add JSDoc comments
```

## Next Steps

After approval:
- If `--tdd`: Write tests first, then implement
- Otherwise: Start implementation
- Use `/review` for code review
- Use `/validate` to verify before completion
- Use `/ship` when ready to commit


ARGUMENTS: Okay, now it's time to deal with our massive EKF divergence. Our plan is to collect data using the crrcsim-smol simulator. The sim can publish sensor messages and truth state messagse using UDP. The protocol is defined in the @lib/sil-protocol/ submodule. We own the crrcsim-smol project and the sil-protocol library, so we can make changes to all 3 simulataneously if necessary. All are in a clean state, on their main branch. The goals are as following:
1. Connect to the crrcsim-smol simulator and receive sensor messages and truth state messages using the hal_native_sil.cpp. 
2. Publish servo messages to the simulator at full rate (100Hz). The sim runs in lockstop, so it requires a servo messages before it can proceed to the next physics calculation.
3. I will fly the aircraft in manual mode.
4. I should be able to connect to the sim aircraft using our GCS.
5. Log the sensor messages, truth state, and the EKF state,  so we can compare our EKF output to the truth state. This requires a way to start logging and stop logging.
6. After the flight, replay the log and compare with plots.

Remember, we can modify all the code in these repos. We can make breaking changes. And use the code-writing-guidelines when writing code.

---

[Request interrupted by user for tool use]

---

I don't think you're understanding how crrcsim gets its joystick input. the original way (before we modified crrcsim), was that the sim would directly connect to the USB joystick and read the input. It had no SIL capabilities, it was just a "regular" simulator. We have since modified it so that the sim runs in lockstep with the external joystick commands that it receives, send via UDP. Without receiving an RC input message, the sim does not proceed to the next physics step. Rather than have to run a separate terminal with "just joystick" that sends joystick commands to the simulator, I think it makes sense for the smol SIL process to also handle sending RC input messages. It will be sending it to the same location as it's receiving data from. So we need the URL And port to be configurable for the sim, in the event that the sim is ever running on a separate computer

# Slop Command

Check the diff against main and remove all AI-generated slop introduced in this branch.

## What is "Slop"?

AI-generated code often has tells that make it look unnatural:

### 1. Over-Commenting
```typescript
// BAD: AI slop
// Get the user from the database
const user = await db.getUser(id); // Fetch user by ID

// GOOD: Self-documenting, no comment needed
const user = await db.getUser(id);
```

### 2. Defensive Overkill
```typescript
// BAD: Unnecessary defensive checks
function processUser(user: User) {
  if (!user) {
    throw new Error('User is required');
  }
  if (!user.id) {
    throw new Error('User must have an id');
  }
  // ... when caller already validates
}

// GOOD: Trust internal callers
function processUser(user: User) {
  // Just do the work - caller handles validation
}
```

### 3. Type Escapes
```typescript
// BAD: Casting to escape type issues
const data = response as any;
const items = (result as unknown as Item[]);

// GOOD: Fix the actual type
const data: ResponseType = response;
```

### 4. Inconsistent Style
- Different naming conventions than the file uses
- Different error handling patterns
- Different import styles
- Added JSDoc when file doesn't use it (or vice versa)

### 5. Unnecessary Try/Catch
```typescript
// BAD: Wrapping things that don't throw
try {
  const x = a + b;
  return x;
} catch (error) {
  console.error('Failed to add numbers', error);
  throw error;
}

// GOOD: Just do it
return a + b;
```

### 6. Verbose Logging
```typescript
// BAD: Logging everything
console.log('Starting process...');
console.log('User ID:', userId);
console.log('Processing...');
console.log('Done!');

// GOOD: Log meaningful events only (or nothing for simple ops)
```

## Workflow

### 1. Get the Diff

```bash
git diff main...HEAD
```

Identify all files changed in this branch.

### 2. For Each Changed File

1. Read the FULL file (not just the diff) to understand existing patterns
2. Compare new code against existing style:
   - Comment density
   - Error handling approach
   - Naming conventions
   - Type annotation style
   - Import organization

### 3. Identify Slop

Look for code that:
- Has MORE comments than surrounding code
- Has MORE defensive checks than similar code paths
- Uses `any` or type assertions
- Has different formatting/style than the file
- Adds try/catch around non-throwing code
- Adds logging that doesn't match file patterns

### 4. Fix It

Remove or adjust:
- Delete unnecessary comments
- Remove redundant validation (if callers are trusted)
- Fix types properly instead of casting
- Match existing code style
- Remove pointless try/catch
- Remove excessive logging

**Use Edit tool to make changes.**

### 5. Report

End with a **1-3 sentence summary only**:

```
Removed 4 unnecessary comments, 2 redundant null checks, and fixed
1 `any` cast in UserService.ts. Deleted try/catch wrapper in
processPayment() since the caller handles errors.
```

## What NOT to Remove

- Comments that explain non-obvious business logic
- Validation at system boundaries (user input, external APIs)
- Error handling that matches the file's existing patterns
- Logging that matches existing patterns
- Type assertions that are genuinely necessary

## Example

**Before (AI slop):**
```typescript
/**
 * Fetches user data from the database
 * @param userId - The ID of the user to fetch
 * @returns The user object or null if not found
 */
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  // Validate the user ID
  if (!userId) {
    throw new Error('userId is required');
  }

  try {
    // Fetch the user from database
    const user = await db.users.findOne({ id: userId });

    // Return the user
    return user as any as User;
  } catch (error) {
    // Log the error
    console.error('Failed to fetch user:', error);
    throw error;
  }
}
```

**After (cleaned):**
```typescript
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  return db.users.findOne({ id: userId });
}
```

**Report:** "Removed JSDoc (file doesn't use it), deleted redundant userId validation (TypeScript enforces it), removed try/catch (caller handles errors), fixed `any` cast by using proper return type."

## Notes

- Run AFTER implementation, before /review
- Focuses on style consistency, not functionality
- Be conservative - when unsure, leave it
- Check git diff after to verify changes make sense

# Review Command

**Purpose:** Qualitative code review - checks code quality, style, security, and best practices.

**Distinct from /validate:** This command does human-like code review. Use `/validate` for automated checks (types, lint, tests, build).

**Workflow:** `/review` → `/validate` → `/ship`

+static void ParseSimAddress(const char* addr_str) {
+  std::string addr(addr_str);
+  size_t colon = addr.rfind(':');
+  if (colon == std::string::npos) {
+    fprintf(stderr, "FATAL: invalid sim address '%s' (expected host:port)\n", addr_str);
+    exit(1);
+  }
+  std::string host = addr.substr(0, colon);
+  int port = std::stoi(addr.substr(colon + 1));
+
+  sim_addr.sin_family = AF_INET;
+  sim_addr.sin_port = htons(static_cast<uint16_t>(port));
+  if (inet_pton(AF_INET, host.c_str(), &sim_addr.sin_addr) != 1) {
+    fprintf(stderr, "FATAL: invalid IP address '%s'\n", host.c_str());
+    exit(1);
+  }
+  sim_addr_len = sizeof(sim_addr);

# Validate Command

**Purpose:** Quantitative validation - runs automated checks (types, lint, tests, build).

**Distinct from /review:** This command runs automated tooling. Use `/review` first for qualitative code review (style, security, best practices).

**Workflow:** `/review` → `/validate` → `/ship`

Run all validations before shipping code. Automatically detects the project's tech stack and runs only relevant checks.

## 1. Detect Tech Stack

First, check which config files exist to determine the project type:

- `package.json` → Node.js/TypeScript project
- `tsconfig.json` → TypeScript
- `pyproject.toml` or `requirements.txt` → Python
- `Cargo.toml` → Rust
- `go.mod` → Go

Use Glob to check for these files before running language-specific checks.

## 2. Run Relevant Checks

### TypeScript/Node.js (if package.json exists)

This session is being continued from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary below covers the earlier portion of the conversation.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The user's primary goal was to build a SIL (Software-in-the-Loop) simulation pipeline to diagnose EKF divergence by collecting data with ground truth from the CRRCSim simulator. Specific goals:
   - Connect smol flight controller to CRRCSim via UDP lockstep protocol
   - Fly the aircraft manually with a joystick
   - Log sensor data, truth state, and EKF state for comparison
   - Build analysis tools to compare EKF output vs ground truth with plots
   - Replace the ArduPilot replay test with a SIL reference flight regression test
   - Connect GCS to the SIL aircraft (planned but not yet implemented)
   
   The session also included handling PR #34 review comments, creating PR #35, and committing changes to crrcsim-smol.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - **UDP Lockstep Protocol**: CRRCSim blocks on `recv_actuator()` waiting for `SimActuatorMsg`. FC sends actuator, sim runs FDM, sends sensors back. Both sides must respond every cycle.
   - **SIL HAL**: `hal_native_sil.cpp` implements the same `hal::*` API as hardware HAL but over UDP sockets
   - **Truth Sidecar**: Packed `SilTruthRecord` (48 bytes, `#pragma pack(push, 1)`) written 1:1 alongside `FlightLoopSnapshot` (288 bytes)
   - **Manual Mode in Flight Loop**: `ManualControllerUpdate` moved from `CascadeController` to `FlightLoop::Step()` so manual mode works without nav state
   - **Lockstep Keepalive**: `SleepUntilNextCycle()` sends neutral actuator if `WriteServos` wasn't called (tracks via `actuator_sent_this_cycle` flag)
   - **Joystick Architecture**: RC input goes from external Python joystick publisher → UDP `SimRcMsg` → smol SIL `ReadRc()`, not through CRRCSim
   - **sil-protocol**: Shared C header + Python ctypes bindings defining 8 message types (IMU, GPS, MAG, BARO, AIRSPEED, TRUTH, RC, ACTUATOR)
   - **`sigaction` without `SA_RESTART`**: Ensures `recvfrom` returns `EINTR` on Ctrl-C for clean shutdown
   - **`nav.value_or(StateEstimate{})`**: Used in `CreateSnapshot` when nav is nullopt (manual mode without EKF)

3. Files and Code Sections:

   - **`src/flight_loop.cpp`** — Core flight loop changes
     - Manual mode handled before cascade controller (works without nav)
     - `nav.value_or(StateEstimate{})` for snapshot when nav is nullopt
     - `ControlOutput control_output = {};` value-initialized
     ```cpp
     ControlOutput control_output = {};
     if (_active_mode == FlightMode::kManual) {
       control_output = ManualControllerUpdate(rc_in);
     } else if (nav) {
       control_output = _cascade_controller.Update(_active_mode, rc_in, *nav, kCyclePeriodSec);
     } else {
       return true;
     }
     ```

   - **`src/hal/native/hal_native_sil.cpp`** — Complete SIL HAL rewrite
     - Configurable sim address via `ParseSimAddress()`
     - Fixed listen port 9003 (`kSilListenPort`)
     - Handshake with retry (1s timeout, EINTR check for Ctrl-C)
     - Drain remaining handshake messages, send kickoff actuator
     - `SilTruthRecord` packed struct (48 bytes) with `static_assert`
     - Truth sidecar written in `WriteLog()` alongside snapshot
     - `actuator_sent_this_cycle` flag for lockstep keepalive
     - `SleepUntilNextCycle()` sends neutral actuator if WriteServos wasn't called
     - 1Hz status print showing truth state (alt, phi, theta, psi, vn, ve, vd)
     - `strtol` with range validation for port parsing (replaced `std::stoi`)
     - `_find_repo_root()` for sil_protocol.py path resolution
     ```cpp
     #pragma pack(push, 1)
     struct SilTruthRecord {
       float time_sec;
       double latitude_deg;
       double longitude_deg;
       float altitude_m;
       float vn_mps, ve_mps, vd_mps;
       float phi_deg, theta_deg, psi_deg;
     };
     #pragma pack(pop)
     static_assert(sizeof(SilTruthRecord) == 48, "SilTruthRecord must be 48 bytes (packed)");
     ```

   - **`src/main_native_sil.cpp`** — SIL entry point
     - `--sim host:port` argument (default `127.0.0.1:9002`)
     - Auto-creates `validation/sil_logs/YYYY-MM-DD_HH-MM-SS/` session directories
     - `MakeSessionDir()` with `mkdir` error checking (`errno != EEXIST`)
     - `sigaction` without `SA_RESTART` for clean Ctrl-C handling
     - Passes `sim_addr` and `session_dir` to `hal::Init()`

   - **`src/control/cascade_controller.cpp`** — Manual mode removed
     - `kManual` case now has `assert(false)` (unreachable since Step() handles manual)
     - `ManualControllerUpdate` include removed, `<cassert>` added
     - `kAttitudeHold/kCruise/kAuto` return `ControlOutput{}` with `// TODO: Implement`

   - **`validation/sil_compare.py`** — New analysis script
     - Reads snapshot `.bin` + `.truth` sidecar
     - Computes RMS errors (position via `lla_to_ned`, velocity, attitude via `angle_diff_deg`)
     - `--plot` flag for 3x3 grid of EKF vs truth plots
     - Takes `.bin` path, derives `.truth` path by replacing extension

   - **`validation/sil_truth.py`** — New truth file reader
     - `TRUTH_DTYPE` numpy dtype matching packed `SilTruthRecord`
     - `read_truth(path)` returns structured numpy array

   - **`validation/test_replay.py`** — Rewritten as SIL regression test
     - Replaced ArduPilot subprocess replay test with stored SIL reference flight
     - Reads `validation/sil_reference/flight.bin` + `flight.truth`
     - Tight RMS bounds: position <0.5m, velocity <0.5 m/s, attitude <2° (psi <15°)
     - Runs in 0.28s (vs ~2s for old subprocess test)
     ```python
     RMS_BOUNDS: dict[str, float] = {
         "north_m": 0.5, "east_m": 0.5, "altitude_m": 1.0,
         "vn_mps": 0.5, "ve_mps": 0.5, "vd_mps": 0.5,
         "phi_deg": 2.0, "theta_deg": 2.0, "psi_deg": 15.0,
     }
     ```

4. Errors and Fixes:

   - **Lockstep deadlock on first cycle**: `Step()` returned early without calling `WriteServos()` when EKF was initializing and mode was kAuto. CRRCSim never got actuator response.
     - User rejected fix of adding `hal::WriteServos(ServoOutput{})` to flight_loop.cpp: "You're changing the flight_loop to match sil behavior, instead of changing sil behavior to match the flight loop"
     - Fixed by adding `actuator_sent_this_cycle` flag and sending neutral actuator in `SleepUntilNextCycle()` when WriteServos wasn't called

   - **SIL binary couldn't exit during handshake**: `recvfrom` with 1s timeout ignored SIGINT
     - Fixed by checking `errno == EINTR` in handshake loop and calling `exit(0)`
     - Also fixed `signal()` → `sigaction()` without `SA_RESTART` so `recvfrom` returns EINTR

   - **SIL binary hung after handshake**: Handshake consumed sensor messages but didn't properly kick off the lockstep cycle
     - Multiple iterations of handshake logic, debugged with comprehensive diagnostic prints
     - Final solution: simple handshake (send actuator, wait for any reply, drain, send kickoff actuator)

   - **Aircraft not moving**: `WriteServos` sending all zeros despite RC input
     - Root cause: `ManualControllerUpdate` was called in cascade controller which returned `ControlOutput{}` for kManual
     - Fixed by moving manual mode handling to `Step()` before cascade controller

   - **Joystick input not reaching smol**: User corrected understanding that CRRCSim doesn't read SDL joystick in smol protocol mode — `SimRcMsg` just echoes actuator commands
     - Created separate `sil_publisher` that reads pygame joystick and sends `SimRcMsg` directly to smol on port 9003
     - Disabled `sendRc()` in CRRCSim

   - **CRRCSim couldn't reconnect after smol disconnect**: `UdpServerCharDevice::read()` rejected messages from different client address
     - Fixed both `read()` and `read_blocking()` to accept new clients by updating `connectedClientAddr`

   - **Truth data garbled**: `SilTruthRecord` had padding due to `double` alignment after `float`
     - Fixed with `#pragma pack(push, 1)` and `static_assert(sizeof == 48)`

   - **Flake8 pre-commit failures**: `setup.cfg` was accidentally deleted, reverting line length from 99 to default 79
     - Restored `setup.cfg` from HEAD

   - **Joystick controls reversed**: Roll, pitch, yaw needed inverting
     - Fixed by toggling `inverted` flags in `calibration.yaml`

   - **`std::stoi` throws on malformed port**: Replaced with `strtol` + endptr + range check (1-65535)

   - **`mkdir` failures silently ignored**: Added error checking with `errno != EEXIST`

   - **Hardcoded relative path to sil_protocol.py**: Replaced `parent.parent.parent.parent` chain with `_find_repo_root()` that walks up looking for `.git`
